JOE ROGAN: CBD is awesome. Yeah, it’s gigantic. Love it. But for you, I can’t say this enough, you need rigorous exercise. You need something really hard, so when it’s done, you’re f*ing spent.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: Just laying on the ground, can’t breathe, puddle of sweat, that type of shit. You need to exercise the demons.

MILEY CYRUS: I have a seven month German shepherd at home, so that seems like a good, if anyone’s going to be my running partner, that’s who’s going to put me through it.

JOE ROGAN: But you need someone to push you. You need to purge the demons. You got demons?

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, yeah, they’re in there 100%. But again, you don’t want to, you got to hold on to them a little bit.

MILEY CYRUS: I know. I like to use them to my advantage sometimes.

## The Role of Demons in Art

JOE ROGAN: Music, man. There’s something about the demons that come out in the music. I mean, look, that’s always why the great artist, think about Robert Johnson, right? They even thought he sold his soul to learn how to play blues the way he did. And it’s because the f*ing life experience came out in his music.

You need both of those. You can’t be some person who just lives in a f*ing monastery and breathes in and breathes out all day and then put out amazing art.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: You have to have pain and life.

MILEY CYRUS: I know that. And I think that’s, one of our words we’ve used pretty consistently today is balance. I think that’s pretty much got to be my mantra.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah. Well, for you, I mean, you are born into this treacherous path. You have this crazy position that you find yourself thrust into where you’re very famous at a very early age. And also there’s these weird expectations because you’re famous for a Disney show, which is even crazier. And then post Disney show, it’s a whole…

MILEY CYRUS: And then that got erased by craziness and wild and being a provocateur. And so now I feel like I’m breaking out of another role in a way.

JOE ROGAN: You’re becoming just yourself instead of a rebellious person who’s trying to escape the sort of the boundaries of your persona.

## Reclaiming the Music

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, well, that’s why I wanted, in my music video, I have me with the microphone, with the microphone stand. And the reason why that was so important was, I’m not just fing getting naked anymore and swinging around this. It’s about the music comes first. And I feel like people are very visual and if you can hold the fing microphone in your hand and say, “This is who I am. This comes first. By the way, I don’t come without this.”

At the VMAs, they tried to get me to get rid of my microphone for something that I’m going to be doing. And I said, “F*, no.” What do you think? I can’t be Britney Spears with the headset and the snake. What’s important? I don’t want the snake. I don’t want the gag.

And there was actually even some comments that day about, it was just an interesting conversation in regards to lighting because I’ve been kind of learning a lot from directors. I didn’t go to film school, but I have been put through that in that way. So I directed the last video, and that’s what I look forward to doing in the next 10 years. I’d love to write and direct and work on film and that way.

And so now I have a better understanding of cameras and lighting operation. And so I was just asking some questions about, not even on some diva shit, like, “I only want to get shot from this side,” whatever. I wanted the lights to be turned off and that the lighting of the room to be just lighting me. So no key light, no beauty light. And beauty light is always used on women.

And I said, “Turn the f*ing lights off. You would never tell Travis Scott or Adam Levine that he couldn’t turn the beauty light off. I want this red lighting.” They said, “Okay, okay, we’ll do it. Same thing that we would do with the guys.” That’s what I want.

And then something that I was doing, which I can’t say, but something that I was doing for the VMAs, my bracelets kept getting caught and all this shit. And they said, “You wanted to be treated like a guy and lit like a guy. We wouldn’t be dealing with this if a guy was doing it.” And I said, “Well, a guy wouldn’t be doing this because a guy doesn’t sell your show with sex the way that I’m going to. And I’m aware of that. I know about what.” I had these conversations with the directors talking to me.

JOE ROGAN: That’s a ridiculous conversation.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s a ridiculous conversation. Also embarrassing, because once you see what happens on the show, you’ll understand more if you see it. But it might be hard not to. If you take walks like I do, you might see it whether you want to or not. If I usually walk down the street and there’s, I don’t know, maybe people sell magazines I don’t know about. Jamie will pull it up or you’ll see it at some point.

JOE ROGAN: You guys can see it, he’ll show me.

## Pop Culture and Escapism

MILEY CYRUS: So, yes. And so they’re asking a lot of questions about that and, well, how long is glam going to take and all this stuff? And I was like, I mean, I can’t really nail it in enough, too. It’s like, I did come from the world of Dolly Parton, and I love pop culture for entertainment and escapism.

And again, we’re joking about the hoodie conversation, but I mean, for me, there’s nights where I don’t do that. At Chris Cornell, I had on a pair of black pants and a f*ing Chris Cornell T-shirt. That’s what it was. The VMAs is a pop culture show celebrating pop culture. And I wanted to bring, especially in this time of COVID-19, all these at home performance, I want to give my fans escapism. Good old pop culture. This is surrealism.

JOE ROGAN: How hard is it to deal with people that are directing you like that? How hard is it to deal with other people and their vision and they’re talking and they’re this and they’re that, when you are just trying to get out what’s in your head and what your vision is?

## Being Firm and Kind

MILEY CYRUS: I get it done. I get it done. But the balance that I found is firm and kind. I don’t lose my kindness, but also don’t become a mat. But I am firm about what I want, but in a way that, you might expect someone might say, “Man, she was a diva. She was a bitch.”

But it’s again, it’s like, okay, have the Weeknd come in here and say the same thing. And you would say him, or Kanye is a creative God. And it’s like, come on, why am I not getting that? I’m a creative mastermind, but I’m becoming a bitch. It’s like, no one would ever say that about Kanye West choosing what lighting he wants on a performance.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah, it’s such a delicate balance, too, right? Because when someone’s as popular as you, you know what the f* you want to do. And if this person who you’re using as a director, if you don’t have a deep relationship with them, that’s…

MILEY CYRUS: Why I started directing my own shit.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah.

## Creating Music Videos and Relationships

MILEY CYRUS: And that’s why I loved making my last video so much. And directing it was because I thought about my scenes almost like a relationship. You’re having a relationship with it. When it’s over, it’s over. What’s painful isn’t the relationship. It’s that when it’s done, you holding on for that extra however long you try to make it work, something that’s not working. That’s what I did on the video.

And that’s what I hated when I was a kid, you know, from directors not knowing what they want and then getting frustrated with the child for not performing properly. It’s like, but you’re not communicating and I’m a child and you’re an adult and you’re not communicating properly. So you’re working me into the ground to get something that you don’t know what you want. And that was always really frustrating to me.

And I think that’s why now a non-negotiable in my relationship or dating life is you better know what you want. Because I’m just not interested in taking another 10 years like I did with my first love, figuring that out.

## The Creative Process

JOE ROGAN: When you’re doing these, like when you’re putting together music, do you have anybody that, like if you’re doing an album or you have a song, do you collaborate with people? Would you write the songs entirely on your own and bring them to other musicians? How do you construct something?

MILEY CYRUS: It’s been different. So on Bangers, which I kind of think my career as a solo artist, I guess kind of started there. I mean, not really. When I started working, you know, on my very first, first record and it was called Breakout and it was because I was kind of breaking out of the character that I was.

JOE ROGAN: How long ago was this?

MILEY CYRUS: Like 2007, I guess maybe something like that.

JOE ROGAN: Crazy. 2007 years ago. Holy shit.

MILEY CYRUS: 2007. I already had two records out already, but they were as Hannah Montana.

JOE ROGAN: So you were 14.

MILEY CYRUS: I’m 27. Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: That’s bananas.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

## Life on the Road

JOE ROGAN: Okay. So when you’re on Hannah Montana and—

MILEY CYRUS: I already had two albums that were like number one and done all the things. And so then I had this pressure.

JOE ROGAN: How much were you working?

MILEY CYRUS: Every single day.

JOE ROGAN: Every Sunday too?

MILEY CYRUS: Sunday. Every Sunday because I wanted to.

JOE ROGAN: Jesus Christ.

MILEY CYRUS: Sunday because I wanted to all day. I remember one time I came home and my dad almost didn’t let me go back on the road because I was so thin and he was like, “What have you been eating?” I’m like, “Turkey cheese lunchables,” you know? And he’s like, “Holy shit.”

JOE ROGAN: Who’s taking care of you when you’re on the road if it’s not your dad?

MILEY CYRUS: My grandma. My grandma and my mom. My mom has been my—like, my mom is the reason I’m sitting here.

JOE ROGAN: So your mom and your grandma would come with you on the road, and you would just go town to town, arena to arena. Boom, boom, boom, boom, boom. Eat, sleep, wake up. There you go. Here’s the mic. You look beautiful. Go to school. Oh, skip school.

MILEY CYRUS: I did school in the morning.

JOE ROGAN: What kind of school you doing?

MILEY CYRUS: I had my teacher on the road with me. Jesus was the best. Who I loved and loved love.

JOE ROGAN: But no kids.

MILEY CYRUS: What do you mean? No, no. No friends, no other kids. Just my little sister and my little brother.

JOE ROGAN: How weird is that?

MILEY CYRUS: That was pretty weird. It made me—it made my sister’s life a little difficult also, because her idea of like, success is completely blown out of proportion also.

JOE ROGAN: Oh, yeah.

## Family and Fame

MILEY CYRUS: And my brother, too. But my brother is very simple, and I love him so much. And he’ll probably be listening to this. And my brother just has his chickens and his ducks, and he’s in Nashville, and he’s in, you know, small little place, and he’s living more—I sometimes wonder if he’s the smartest of us all. I don’t know.

JOE ROGAN: Maybe has less stress.

MILEY CYRUS: He has less stress.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah. That’s the thing about it.

MILEY CYRUS: But he’s also a f*ing badass talent, but he just saves it. He doesn’t want to be on that level. Like, he wants to make music because he loves it. He wants the people that are interested in him to hear it. He doesn’t have the “I got to grind” mentality.

JOE ROGAN: He has some shit that’s online right now?

MILEY CYRUS: He has some shit that’s online right now.

JOE ROGAN: What’s his name?

MILEY CYRUS: Braison Cyrus.

JOE ROGAN: And how do you get—does he have an Instagram?

MILEY CYRUS: He has an Instagram. He’ll kill me. But he has a Spotify. He has a song out. And he did Fallon. And after he did Fallon, he’s like, “I don’t think I want to do that ever again.” I’m like, “What the—” He’s like, “Man, I was—that was too scary. No, thank you.” And he didn’t. I’m like, “All right.”

JOE ROGAN: Good for him.

MILEY CYRUS: He had two shows. One at CityWalk, Universal down the street. And he said no. Someone said I was fat and my hair was ugly. I’m like, “You know many times I’ve been called—” My hair is ugly. And he’s like, “I’m not ready for that.” He didn’t perform again. Then he’s like, “I’m going to try it again. Fallon.” I’m like, “You’re going to go from Universal CityWalk to Fallon? Whatever.”

So I go there and I try to change his shirt, and he’s like, “No, this is me. I’m wearing my flannel,” you know, the whole thing. So he goes out and kills it and he goes, “Uh, not for me.” Wow.

JOE ROGAN: Well, you know, maybe growing up and seeing all the crazy shit that happened to you, it’s almost like growing up around an alcoholic and never wanting to drink.

MILEY CYRUS: Exactly. You can go one way or the other, right? You either become my little sister who kind of wants it, you know, and she’s got a record out that I love called The End of Everything.

JOE ROGAN: What’s her name?

MILEY CYRUS: Noah Cyrus. And it’s the most depressing EP you’ll ever listen to. She’s 20 years old.

JOE ROGAN: It’s depressing?

MILEY CYRUS: She’s emo. She’s like an emo kid.

JOE ROGAN: Why is she emo? Maybe because she was on the road.

MILEY CYRUS: She has a song where she says, “My sister’s like sunshine and it’ll follow her wherever she goes. But I’m more like a rain cloud,” you know? It’s like she’s really got this idea of me. She needs to go to the doctor. She is. We’re all at the doctor a lot. We have like a salaried doctor that just—

JOE ROGAN: Oh, boy.

MILEY CYRUS: We got to deal with that. Yeah, she’s dealing with it. She’s dealing with it. But she’s only 20, so I worry about it.

JOE ROGAN: It’s the hardest age for kids today, too. It’s so hard.

MILEY CYRUS: Dude, if you don’t look like these girls on Instagram right now—

JOE ROGAN: They don’t even look like these girls.

MILEY CYRUS: I know.

## The Filter Problem

JOE ROGAN: Want to see something crazy?

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, I do.

JOE ROGAN: My 10-year-old did—we were in a restaurant. She took a picture of me. My 10-year-old thinks it’s f*ing hilarious when she does this. You know where it is, Jamie, right? That—he’ll put it up on the screen. She took a picture of me and she goes, “Let me take a picture of you. Make a face.” I made this great crazy kissy face. And then she put it through this filter. That’s me.

MILEY CYRUS: No.

JOE ROGAN: Yes.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s not real.

JOE ROGAN: That’s real. That’s me. That’s me through a filter.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s not real.

JOE ROGAN: That’s me. Are you real?

MILEY CYRUS: Are you f*ing kidding me?

JOE ROGAN: That’s how bad these goddamn filters are. What’s wrong with your—I don’t know what’s happening. Okay, so that’s the original picture, right? That’s me and her at a restaurant. And that’s what came out. And meanwhile, do you know my 10-year-old, she’s f*ing hilarious. She thinks it’s so funny.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s not right.

JOE ROGAN: That is how fed up these goddamn filters are. It’s just a filter on an app. That’s why these girls are so insecure, because they think all these people that they see online are perfect, but every one of those bitches is using filters. All of them. All of them, all of them. And even people that I’m friends with that contacted me, like, “This is crazy. I use filters.” But that—f, that’s f*ing—

MILEY CYRUS: So I don’t have a filter on my phone. And I need to know, though, what your daughter is using. Like, I don’t even understand this technology.

JOE ROGAN: It’s trickery. It’s witchcraft. It’s f*ing trickery.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: I couldn’t believe that was real.

MILEY CYRUS: The only thing I have on my phone is where I can swipe on the Instagram story thingy and turn Paris, you know, where it kind of blurs out your pores or something. That’s all I got.

JOE ROGAN: Don’t even use that. It’s ridiculous.

MILEY CYRUS: It looks pretty good.

JOE ROGAN: No, you look great. You don’t need that shit. No, it makes you look like a cartoon. It doesn’t make you look—

MILEY CYRUS: I don’t do any of the shit.

JOE ROGAN: Girls want that. They want like, no flaws. They want everything to be like, cloudy.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s basically what it does. It makes you look like a punk.

JOE ROGAN: But that’s not good.

MILEY CYRUS: I know, I know. There’s so much unprogramming to do on me.

JOE ROGAN: There’s so much on everybody.

MILEY CYRUS: There’s so much unprogramming.

JOE ROGAN: It’s all these weird things out there that are these unrealistic expectations. Like, I’m sure you saw that Khloe Kardashian picture that looks nothing like her.

MILEY CYRUS: Where it like, goes from like, the hairline, like, nonsense.

JOE ROGAN: They used Photoshop on her. I mean, it’s like CGI. You might as well be looking at a monster movie. Like she turns into a werewolf. It’s not what—that’s not who she is.

## Reality vs. Social Media

MILEY CYRUS: No, no. It’s crazy. And even like, for me, I think, you know, in my real life, I don’t wear any makeup. I don’t even—like, today someone asked me, “What do you use on your hair?” And I’m like, “Shampoo and conditioner.” Like, I don’t do anything to my hair. I don’t really do anything.

And that’s been really f*ing tough for me over the last few months, too, because I don’t know why. I guess I think as that keeps happening, like, as these technology things keep happening on Instagram, these filters keep getting better and better. I’m compared to the people altering themselves either physically with all these things you can do and lasers and all the shit, or to the filters.

And I’ve had a really hard time with that. And I think it’s hard for me. The other day, you know, I get papped walking around my neighborhood in like, a really shitty, dirty Fleetwood Mac T-shirt that I’ve been in for five days, and it hurts.

JOE ROGAN: Just don’t go online. Just detox from all that shit.

MILEY CYRUS: No wifi, like Braison.

JOE ROGAN: Just don’t pay attention to all these other women that are doing these fing wacky filters, because that’s where everybody gets fed up. It’s the comparison thing. There’s a book called The Coddling of the American Mind by Jonathan Haidt, and he talks about young girls and depression, this gigantic uptick in depression that directly coincides with the invention of the iPhone.

And that as the iPhone came up and then pictures and then social media apps—so at first it was a lot of it was social media and people being mean to each other on Twitter and all those things because you’re not seeing each other.

MILEY CYRUS: There’s something about the iPhone kind of, I guess, mimicking, right, Vegas slot machines and things.

JOE ROGAN: Oh, yeah.

## Social Media Addiction and the Slot Machine Effect

MILEY CYRUS: Like, it’s actually. Isn’t it? I think it was called, what I listened to was the slot machine in your pocket.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah, well, it is a lot like that. But the thing about it with women in particular with young girls, is that they’re comparing themselves to these cartoons, these people that don’t even really like that picture of me.

MILEY CYRUS: You know, when I got sober, I had to delete all the apps on my phone where I could purchase things. Like, I had to take off Amazon and all the things on my phone because walking around with that slot machine in my pocket, all of a sudden I’m getting these bills and things. And yes, I care about that, and I want to live financially responsible and all the things.

And I’m looking at this, I’m like, I don’t even remember doing this. Like, it’s totally like being high on drugs. It is. And things started showing up, and you’re like, what the hell? It’s too easy.

JOE ROGAN: I’m in the middle of a book now about that. It’s called “Irresistible.” Let me find that. It’s on my Instagram, too. Jamie. “Irresistible” is this book that is about how people are addicted. It’s by Adam Alter, and it’s about how people are addicted to your phones and applications.

But it also goes into just the actual physical aspect of addiction and how it works on the brain and how we always think of addiction as, it’s something that you get hooked physically and you can’t live without it. No. It’s something that you have a compulsion to use, and you can’t avoid that compulsion for some reason. And it doesn’t even necessarily have to be good.

## Love as an Addiction

MILEY CYRUS: No. And it can happen with things like love. And I’ve even felt that, too. And it’s in the most stressful times of my life, it’s okay, I can’t reach for drugs anymore. Okay. I don’t want to reach for bad food. All right? I’m going to reach for someone to love me. And it’s coming down from something all the time.

JOE ROGAN: Well, the beginning part of love is the most powerful drug you’re ever going to take.

MILEY CYRUS: It’s like cocaine.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah. It’s dopamine. Straight dopamine. Right to the f*ing veins.

MILEY CYRUS: Dr. Amen has a book, “Brain in Love,” and I read it a lot because I had a tendency to need someone in my life at all times. And I actually now, I really love just factual information. So you can go, I’m not a total freak that’s got this. I’m not a love addict. This is actually what is happening to me on a level of, this is uncontrollable. You can control how it affects you and what you’re, I guess, kind of learn to control your reaction.

JOE ROGAN: Exactly. You can control your reaction.

MILEY CYRUS: But when you love someone the first couple of months, you do feel like you’re high on drugs.

JOE ROGAN: It is.

MILEY CYRUS: It is literally the same drip.

JOE ROGAN: It really is. It’s dopamine.

MILEY CYRUS: And I kind of, he writes how it kind of goes from more like cocaine, which is kind of a quick and wears off really quickly, so you need a lot of it. And then it becomes more like heroin, where it’s something that almost soothes you.

Actually, I called the love of mine, who I was with, and we got divorced. It was almost like a pacifier. Like, it was that thing that I just needed. Not because we were in love anymore, but because of the comfort and because my brain said, oh, this feels better. This is comforting.

But actually knowing that I was giving in to an addiction made me feel way worse. I had the hangover. Next day, okay, we sleep together. Next day we wake up, I’m totally hungover. Yeah, it felt like a relapse every time I go back.

JOE ROGAN: Well, people do it to each other. You know, it’s not even anybody’s fault. It’s you don’t even realize that you’re a part of this drug cycle. And then you get involved in that, and then you find some new person and you get lit up.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: Maybe some new person you see at the gym or at the office or wherever you meet people, and you’re like.

## Avoiding Success Metrics

MILEY CYRUS: Well, what’s funny about this is, I guess I just realized something myself is all of a sudden, it’s unavoidable. I’m telling you, this is not true. So this is where I now retract what I’ve said, because I need to work on this a little bit. So it’s okay. It’s so untrue for me to see all these bad things. They’re in my face no matter what. No matter what. I want to look at it or not.

I have a really hard time looking at the good things. When people send me the stats of my song, I don’t open it. When people send me the charts of the views, I don’t open it. That’s a good sign because I don’t want to get attached to success or numbers or meaning that my art, everyone said, literally, I’ll show you the text of a manager. He said, “Unless it’s a drag queen death dropping to her new single, don’t even bother sending it to her because she’s not going to open it.” And I think that’s good.

JOE ROGAN: That’s a sign of you avoiding narcissism.

MILEY CYRUS: But I wonder why I feel like I can avoid, I can’t avoid the bad things and looking at them. Maybe a little addiction of that. Of looking at that. But then why don’t I want the hit of the positivity of seeing the numbers?

JOE ROGAN: Because you want to work hard because you want things to be difficult when you see too much success, you don’t want to slack off.

MILEY CYRUS: I have no idea how many people listen my song.

JOE ROGAN: I have the same thing.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, I can’t.

JOE ROGAN: Same thing. I have the same thing with podcasts. I have the same thing with comedy specials. I don’t read any of the reviews. I just keep moving.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s what I always do that. And everyone’s like, you want to hear some stats? I’m like, I literally, you can ask them. I say, I won’t even know what it means.

JOE ROGAN: Jamie will tell me some stats every now and then. I’ll just go, what the f* is what? Well, it gets nuts.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah. I don’t know what it means.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah. What does it mean?

MILEY CYRUS: And a lot of the time, 3 million streams. What does that mean in the world of how many? 7 billion. It’s never good enough for me. Doesn’t mean I’m 3 million, 7 billion. I could do better, right?

JOE ROGAN: Exactly.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah. 3 million is not enough.

JOE ROGAN: Well, I think that’s a sign that you’re looking at things the right way. I really do. Because I think that’s a sign of you, what you were talking about earlier. You want to struggle. You want to earn it. Because you think that you kind of got these crazy gifts, being famous at a young age and all this wealth and success. Young age. You want to earn it.

So when you see success and the trappings of success or wallowing around in all of your fortune, you don’t want to do that. You want to hustle, you want to keep going. I think that’s a good sign. Yeah, I really do.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah. Yeah. That’s why, yeah. At some point, you can bring your kids. Maybe she can do that weird, f*ed up thing to my face. Whatever. You should come and see some of the animals. Especially when you’re in Nashville. I think you’ll totally get it. I think you’ll totally get. If you’re ever in Tennessee and you out to the farm and you see the horses and you see the pigs bite my ankles and all these things, I’m sure I think you’ll get a really good understanding of my life and who I am.

## Malibu and Creative Process

JOE ROGAN: My last comedy special that I filmed was “Strange Times” for Netflix. And when I warm up for shows, I’ve done all the work, I put my brain in another place. And I was listening to “Malibu.”

MILEY CYRUS: That’s what I thought you were going to say.

JOE ROGAN: All the people on the set were making fun of me so hard. My friend Anthony Giordano who also directs the UFC, by the way.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, I couldn’t imagine that good friend.

JOE ROGAN: He’s what are you listening to? I go, Miley Cyrus. And he’s shut the f* up. I go, look, I go, listen to it. I put the headsets on him and I had him listen to it. But that song is so removed from anything in me or my life. And I love your voice.

MILEY CYRUS: Thank you.

JOE ROGAN: So it’s a little escape for me.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s cool.

JOE ROGAN: So I’d be dancing backstage high as f*, getting ready to go on stage, listening to your song.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, well, that was the first song. That was the first song.

JOE ROGAN: Song.

MILEY CYRUS: Well, no, because I had done “Dead Petz.” “Dead Petz” was where I started writing my music where, if you look at the list, it says, because what’s funny. Okay, so if you look at Stevie Nicks songs, things have changed a lot in credits. A lot of it says written by Stevie Nicks, and it doesn’t says any other writers, but there are other writers because there’s music that was written. She didn’t play every guitar part and every piano part.

Now it’s changed in our credits and the way we do things. So actually you have to put written by for anyone that wrote anything musical on the song. So any guitar parts, all that. So if you start looking at some of the “Dead Petz” stuff, it’ll say written by and it’ll say a group of people, but all the lyrics were written by me. It’s just any of the melodic stuff in the track.

## The Music Industry and Streaming

JOE ROGAN: Is that all stuff that’s new for money purposes?

MILEY CYRUS: I think the way that now streaming is kind of making things a little bit more difficult because you don’t pay someone the way that you would record when record sales, they get their money, whatever, so that it’s something to do with that. And it’s very complex. And they say that some of the best lawyers don’t even understand quite what’s going on in the music industry right now. Because we’re having such change, such a shift in the way that everything’s happening.

JOE ROGAN: From sales of records, sales of records.

MILEY CYRUS: To streaming, to videos, to TikToks. TikTok is like a freaking label now. So they pay TikTokers to TikTok to your music because it counts as streams. I don’t even understand it. I don’t even understand it, but this is a thing.

JOE ROGAN: TikTok is weird. Do you pay attention? All that with, it’s the Chinese government owns it.

MILEY CYRUS: No, I mean, I know that that’s a thing. I also know that it was, this is the new way of the new label. Basically, labels pay TikTok to be able to have these kids doing, I don’t know if I’m supposed to say it, but I do. So then I said it.

JOE ROGAN: Please say it.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s all I know is it’s true. So say it.

JOE ROGAN: So they pay kids to TikTok to certain. So say if you’re a TikToker, you’re a big time TikToker rich.

MILEY CYRUS: TikTokers that are from millions. I don’t know about millions. We have maybe a different idea of Richie Rich, but for kids living in a house here that there’s TikTok agencies.

JOE ROGAN: Yes, TikTok agencies. So they Marcia, I see you TikToking. Why don’t we make a big mirror?

MILEY CYRUS: It’s like a mirror. I’m telling you. It’s some f*ed up Black Mirror.

JOE ROGAN: Wow, Interesting. I didn’t know that.

MILEY CYRUS: But the one thing that I told the kids that, these kind of influencers, I’ve spoken to some of them before by doing some of this press, they want me to play the song for them, whatever. And the one thing that I said that I like is at least it’s kids creating content for themselves. Because I used to have to go through all the middlemen before. Before I could put out a f*ing video. I had to ask, hey, Gary Marsh at Disney, is this okay? Hey, this person, can I do this now? It’s, grab your phone, put it up. You’re in control of your own destiny, right?

## Live Streaming and Creative Freedom

JOE ROGAN: You could. I mean, if you wanted to, you could set your phone up and just go live on YouTube and play an acoustic set and do whatever.

MILEY CYRUS: I love that about that.

JOE ROGAN: So I love that about today.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah, me too. I love that. And yeah, so kind of to that point was when I was working on Younger Now, that was the first record I was going to put out that was for sale. Because I did SoundCloud with my Flaming Lips record. I said people don’t want to hear me singing a song called “Bang My Box” about me having sex at a lesbian strip club. Well, then I’m not going to ask them to buy it. I’m just going to give it to them as a gift. And the worst thing they can do with a gift is throw it away or not open it.

JOE ROGAN: Well, that’s the thing of being in a position where you’re in that you could call the shots.

MILEY CYRUS: Exactly. And it’s like, listen, okay, you’re not going to make money off of it. That’s fine. I’m sure they’re still selling a toothbrush somewhere that plays my f*ing song. And I’ll get a dollar from that.

JOE ROGAN: Are there any TikTokers out there to “Bang My Box”?

MILEY CYRUS: I don’t think anyone’s TikToking to “Bang My Box.”

JOE ROGAN: Jamie, can you research that, please?

MILEY CYRUS: I honestly, I think everything on the Internet’s been done, but I don’t think people TikTok to “Bang My Box.”

JOE ROGAN: I would love to see a bunch of RuPaul’s Drag Queens TikToking to “Bang My Box.”

MILEY CYRUS: I don’t think it’s happening. “Bang My Box” is very, very, very niche.

JOE ROGAN: We can make that happen. I feel like we could put that out there into the Internet now. I’m trying to find a good version to show. I’m trying to be quick about it.

MILEY CYRUS: I’m scared.

JOE ROGAN: Well, listen, Jamie can find it if it’s out there. He has connections to the dark, dark web.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s what I was wondering. You got that hooked up here into the ground.

JOE ROGAN: He’s the best Googler on the planet. There’s no one even close. Yes, he’s a one handed best Googler too.

MILEY CYRUS: I know. Look at this.

JOE ROGAN: He Googles with one hand while he’s working the camera with the other.

MILEY CYRUS: Oh my God.

JOE ROGAN: Let me give me some volume. Let me hear a little bit. Look at this guy. So we got a dude.

MILEY CYRUS: Oh, okay.

JOE ROGAN: There you go.

MILEY CYRUS: Look, this is how sht it is. It’s got two fing likes.

JOE ROGAN: Listen, for now it has two likes. Now people know about it. Now it’ll have more.

MILEY CYRUS: Now he’s an influencer.

JOE ROGAN: I’ll retweet that sh*t later. Send that to me and I’ll retweet it.

## Writing “Malibu” and Family Vacations

MILEY CYRUS: I want you to bang my box. But point being is that that was free. And then getting to write Younger Now and writing “Malibu.” I wrote that in the back of the car on the way to the Voice because I was looking outside the window in the car thinking all of it’s true. I had never really gone to the beach. The closest I ever really gotten was my parents taking me to Florida one time and my sister got my toe caught in the revolving door and I had to go to the hospital and it was a nightmare.

And my parents swore we’d never go on vacation again. But most parents say it and don’t mean it. My parents f*ing meant it. We never went on vacation.

JOE ROGAN: That’s crazy that you did all that work and you never went on vacation.

MILEY CYRUS: Well, I went on my own vacations. We didn’t go on a family vacation.

## The Power of Authentic Songwriting

JOE ROGAN: That song is so obviously written by you.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: And that was one of the things that I think I liked about it, that it was when you listen to someone sing a song, a really good song, it’s an expression of who they are at that point in time in their life, and you can get wrapped up in their mind. And I felt like that’s why I like listening to other people. I like listening to songs before I go on stage because it gets me out of my own head and it gets me into someone else’s head.

And then when it’s time to go, and they’re like, you’re on in three. And then I’ll take the headphones off, I’ll do a shot, I’ll stretch out a little, and then here we go. That’s me.

MILEY CYRUS: Oh, hell yeah.

JOE ROGAN: That is. That’s me listening to your f*ing song backstage.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s crazy.

JOE ROGAN: Yeah, legit. I’m not lying.

MILEY CYRUS: That’s nuts. Well, it’s an honor.

JOE ROGAN: I play that when Anthony was listening to it. He’s like, you f*ing idiot. What are you listening to?

MILEY CYRUS: That’s f*ing wild. I never, ever, ever would have thought that. Would have thought that.

JOE ROGAN: I like it.

MILEY CYRUS: Thank you.

JOE ROGAN: I like your music.

MILEY CYRUS: Thank you.

JOE ROGAN: And I like you. You’re a good person.

MILEY CYRUS: Thank you so much. You too. I enjoyed talking to you.

JOE ROGAN: I did, too. I’m glad we did this.

MILEY CYRUS: Agreed.

## “Midnight Sky” and the Disco Ball Metaphor

JOE ROGAN: So you got something that’s out right now.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah.

JOE ROGAN: What is it? How do people get it?

MILEY CYRUS: Well, it’s called “Midnight Sky,” and even just the title is kind of inspired by Debbie Harry’s “Heart of Glass,” but I pulled inspiration from Edges 17. Two of my favorite songs, “Heart of Glass,” the reason I love it so much is that the title isn’t the repetition in the chorus. It’s just a cool thing to say. It’s not the chorus at all.

And so I thought, you know what my favorite part about it is? I love the kind of visual painting of midnight sky and what that means. And the midnight sky, to me is if you’re really f*ing partying, the moon is a disco ball, and the stars are all the reflection of light on the ceiling.

And what I really like about the disco ball is that it’s a bunch of broken pieces put back together again that when you’re finally enlightened, it makes this mesmerizing, totally attractive. People love disco balls, but it’s really just a bunch of broken pieces put together. And so I felt like that was reflective of me.

JOE ROGAN: Wow.

MILEY CYRUS: Pretty deep. Think about it.

JOE ROGAN: That’s heavy.

MILEY CYRUS: Yeah. When I saw it, I thought I recognize this. This is what I feel like.

JOE ROGAN: All right, so that’s it. Send it on that.

MILEY CYRUS: And it’s everywhere. It’s on YouTube streaming, and yeah, it’s everywhere. And I’m making it so hopefully people will watch it.

JOE ROGAN: All right. You’re a bad motherf*er.

MILEY CYRUS: Thank you. You too.

JOE ROGAN: Thank you.

MILEY CYRUS: Thanks.

JOE ROGAN: Bye, everybody.

MILEY CYRUS: Cool. I like being in here.
